## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology (population dynamics / growth models)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is a time-derivative of population size P, indicating a continuous-time population dynamics (ODE) setting. Typical relationships include per-capita growth, density dependence (crowding), Allee effects at low density, harvesting/immigration terms, and explicit time-varying rates or carrying capacity via t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited resources; constant per-capita rate)
- Linear growth/decline with immigration/emigration: dP_dt = c0 + c1 * P (net constant input plus proportional growth/decay)
- Quadratic density dependence (self-limitation): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (crowding reduces growth; simplest carrying-capacity-like form)
- Logistic ODE (factored form): dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - P) (growth with a fixed carrying scale; equilibria at P=0 and P=c1)
- Theta-logistic (generalized crowding): dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - P**c2) (flexible density dependence; c2 tunes how sharply limitation appears)
- Gompertz growth (log-density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (per-capita growth declines ~log(P); often used for microbial/tumor growth)
- Richards / generalized logistic rate form: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - P)**c2 (adjusts approach-to-asymptote shape beyond simple logistic)
- Allee effect (strong Allee with upper limitation): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (c2 - P) (negative growth below threshold c1; saturation/limit near c2)
- Von Bertalanffy / metabolic scaling growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (sublinear production vs proportional loss; common in growth/energetics contexts)
- Harvesting or proportional removal added to growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - P) - c2 * P (crowding plus exploitation/mortality proportional to P)
- Seasonally forced growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P * (c4 - P) (periodic environment modulates intrinsic rate)
- Time-varying carrying capacity or trend: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 + c2 * t - P) (capacity changes over time due to habitat trend; linear-in-time proxy)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Presence of an overall factor P in dP_dt suggests modeling per-capita growth: (dP_dt) / P depends on P and/or t rather than absolute P alone.
- Multiple equilibria are indicated by factored polynomial forms in P (e.g., P*(c1-P), P*(P-c1)*(c2-P)); each root corresponds to a steady population level.
- A negative P**2 (or higher-power) term in dP_dt indicates crowding/competition; the smallest power producing a carrying effect is quadratic.
- A (P - c) factor implies an Allee threshold: growth becomes negative for P below c, creating potential extinction bistability.
- A log(c / P) term indicates Gompertz-type slowdown: per-capita growth decreases roughly linearly with log(P), often giving asymmetric sigmoidal trajectories.
- Explicit t in coefficients (e.g., c0 + c1*t or exp(c*t) factors) encodes nonstationary environments where intrinsic growth or capacity changes over time.
- Sin(c*t + phase) modulation is a hallmark of seasonal/periodic forcing; it typically produces oscillations around an underlying density-dependent attractor.
- Additive constants in dP_dt (e.g., +c0) represent immigration/stocking (if positive) or constant-yield harvesting (if negative), shifting equilibria away from P=0.

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG5)

GT: c0*(c1 - P/c2)*P + c3*P**c4/(c5*P + c6)
Candidate formulas: 50

Let \(P\) be the only effective variable in the GT (since GT has no \(t\)-dependence). Rewrite the GT into a simple rational-polynomial form:

\[
\text{GT}(P)=0.9198344660\,(1-\tfrac{P}{84.0283518631})P \;+\; 0.9198344660\,\frac{P^2}{7.5314755755\,P+1}.
\]

Expand the first part:
\[
0.9198344660\,P - 0.9198344660\frac{P^2}{84.0283518631}
= aP + bP^2
\]
where \(a=0.9198344660\) and \(b=-0.9198344660/84.0283518631\neq 0\).

So GT is:
\[
\text{GT}(P)= aP + bP^2 + d\frac{P^2}{\alpha P+1}
\]
with \(d=0.9198344660\), \(\alpha=7.5314755755\).

Key structural facts:
- Exactly one rational term of the form \(\dfrac{P^2}{\alpha P+1}\) (linear denominator).
- Plus a polynomial \(aP+bP^2\).
- No constant term, no \(P^3\) term, no \(t\), no exponentials/sines/abs, no \((P+\cdot)^{-5}\).

Now check candidates.

---

### 1
Has terms with denominator \((P+c1)\): \(P^3/(P+c1)\), \(P^2/(P+c1)\), \(P/(P+c1)\), plus polynomial \(P^2\) and \(P\).
You can combine the \((P+c1)\) terms into \(\frac{A P^3 + B P^2 + C P}{P+c1}\).
To match GT’s rational term \(\frac{dP^2}{\alpha P+1}\), we’d set \(c1=1/\alpha\). But then the numerator must be exactly proportional to \(P^2\), i.e. no \(P^3\) and no \(P\) in the numerator ⇒ force \(A=0\) and \(C=0\). That is achievable by setting the corresponding coefficients to 0. Then the remaining polynomial part can match \(aP+bP^2\) by choosing \(c2,c5,c6\).
So **possible**.

### 2
Form: polynomial \(P^2 c0 + P c5 + P c6\) plus several \((P+c2)^{-1}\) terms: \(P^2/(P+c2)\) and \(P/(P+c2)\).
As with (1), combine to \(\frac{A P^2 + B P}{P+c2}\). GT needs only \(P^2/(P+c2)\) (no \(P/(P+c2)\)), so set \(B=0\) by zeroing those coefficients. Then match \(c2=1/\alpha\), match polynomial \(aP+bP^2\) via \(c0,c5,c6\), and match rational coefficient via \(A\).
So **possible**.

### 3
Contains \(c2\exp(c3\sin(\cdot))\), a non-rational non-polynomial term in \(P\). Only way to remove is set \(c2=0\), leaving \(P^2 c0 + Pc1\), which cannot reproduce the GT rational term. **Impossible**.

### 4

There is no free standalone \(P^2\) polynomial term unless it comes from division, but division produces also constants etc unless carefully arranged. I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) and determine which candidates can match it.

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT is:
$$f(P) = 0.9198(1 - P/84.03)P + 0.9198 \cdot P^2/(7.531P + 1)$$

Expanding:
$$f(P) = 0.9198P - 0.01095P^2 + 0.9198P^2/(7.531P + 1)$$

This is a function of P only (no t dependence). Let me write it in general form with free constants:

$$f(P) = aP + bP^2 + \frac{dP^2}{eP + f}$$

This has the structure: **linear in P** + **quadratic in P** + **rational function P²/(linear in P)**.

Let me combine over a common denominator with denominator $(eP + f)$:

$$f(P) = \frac{aP(eP+f) + bP^2(eP+f) + dP^2}{eP+f}$$
$$= \frac{aeP^2 + afP + beP^3 + bfP^2 + dP^2}{eP+f}$$
$$= \frac{beP^3 + (ae + bf + d)P^2 + afP}{eP+f}$$

So the GT is a rational function: $\frac{\alpha P^3 + \beta P^2 + \gamma P}{eP + f}$ (no constant term in numerator, no t dependence).

Key structural features:
1. **No t dependence** - any candidate with t that can't be zeroed out is NO MATCH
2. The function equals 0 when P = 0
3. It's a ratio of a cubic polynomial in P over a linear polynomial in P (with no constant term in numerator)

Let me now systematically check each candidate. For candidates with the right structure, I need to verify they can represent: $\frac{\alpha P^3 + \beta P^2 + \gamma P}{\delta P + \epsilon}$

For candidates that are sums of terms with denominator $(P + c)$ and polynomial terms, I'll combine over the common denominator.

**General approach for candidates with structure: polynomial in P + rational terms with denominator (P+c):**

The GT combined form is: $\frac{beP^3 + (ae+bf+d)P^2 + afP}{eP+f}$

This has 4 free parameters (a, b, d, e with f absorbed by scaling).

Let me work through each candidate:

### Candidate 1:
$$\frac{c_0 P^3}{P+c_1} + c_2 P^2 + \frac{c_3 P^2}{P+c_1} + \frac{c_4 P^2}{P+c_1} + c_5 P + c_6 P + \frac{c_7 P}{P+c_1} + \frac{c_8 P}{P+c_1}$$

Combining $c_3+c_4 \to C_3$, $c_5+c_6 \to C_5$, $c_7+c_8 \to C_7$:

$$= c_2 P^2 + C_5 P + \frac{c_0 P^3 + C_3 P^2 + C_7 P}{P+c_1}$$

Common denominator:
$$= \frac{c_2 P^2(P+c_1) + C_5 P(P+c_1) + c_0 P^3 + C_3 P^2 + C_7 P}{P+c_1}$$
$$= \frac{(c_2+c_0)P^3 + (c_2 c_1 + C_5 + C_3)P^2 + (C_5 c_1 + C_7)P}{P+c_1}$$

This gives $\frac{AP^3 + BP^2 + CP}{P+c_1}$ with 4 free parameters (A, B, C, c_1). This matches the GT structure perfectly.

**Candidate 1 verdict: [MATCH]**

### Candidate 2:
$$c_0 P^2 + \frac{(c_1+c_3)P^2}{P+c_2} + \frac{(c_4+c_7+c_8)P}{P+c_2} + (c_5+c_6)P$$

Common denominator:
$$= \frac{c_0 P^2(P+c_2) + (c_5+c_6)P(P+c_2) + (c_1+c_3)P^2 + (c_4+c_7+c_8)P}{P+c_2}$$
$$= \frac{c_0 P^3 + [c_0 c_2 + c_5+c_6 + c_1+c_3]P^2 + [(c_5+c_6)c_2 + c_4+c_7+c_8]P}{P+c_2}$$

Same structure: $\frac{AP^3+BP^2+CP}{P+c_2}$. Matches.

**Candidate 2 verdict: [MATCH]**

### Candidate 3:
$$c_0 P^2 + c_1 P + c_2 \exp(c_3 \sin(c_4 P + c_5))$$

Contains $\exp(\sin(...))$ which is a transcendental function that cannot equal a rational function. Even setting $c_2=0$ leaves only $c_0 P^2 + c_1 P$, which is a polynomial, not a rational function matching GT.

**Candidate 3 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 4:
$$\frac{c_0 P^3}{P+c_1} + \frac{(c_2+c_3)P^2}{P+c_1} + \frac{(c_4+c_5)P}{P+c_1} + c_6 P + \frac{c_7 P}{P+c_8}$$

This has TWO different denominators: $(P+c_1)$ and $(P+c_8)$. The GT has only one pole. If $c_8 = c_1$, then it reduces to one denominator and works. But $c_8$ is a free constant, so we CAN set $c_8 = c_1$. Alternatively, set $c_7 = 0$.

With $c_7 = 0$: $\frac{c_0 P^3 + (c_2+c_3)P^2 + (c_4+c_5)P}{P+c_1} + c_6 P$

Common denominator: $\frac{c_0 P^3 + (c_2+c_3+c_6)P^2 + (c_4+c_5+c_6 c_1)P}{P+c_1}$

This matches the GT structure.

**Candidate 4 verdict: [MATCH]**

### Candidate 5:
Same as Candidate 1 but with $+c_9$ constant term. The GT has no constant term (f(0)=0). The numerator would have a constant term $c_9(P+c_1)$ contributing $c_9 c_1$ when P=0. But we can set $c_9=0$.

With $c_9=0$, same as Candidate 1.

### Candidate 27:
$$c_0 P^2 + c_1 P + \frac{c_2 P}{c_3 P+1} + c_4 t/(P+c_5)^5$$

Setting $c_4=0$: $c_0 P^2 + c_1 P + \frac{c_2 P}{c_3 P+1}$

This is $c_0 P^2 + c_1 P + \frac{c_2 P}{c_3 P + 1}$. Common denominator:

$\frac{c_0 c_3 P^3 + (c_0+c_1 c_3)P^2 + (c_1+c_2)P}{c_3 P+1}$

This has the form $\frac{AP^3+BP^2+CP}{DP+E}$ with 5 effective parameters (A,B,C,D,E but one can be absorbed by scaling, so 4 independent). The GT needs 4 parameters. Let me check if the constraints are satisfiable.

GT: $\frac{be \cdot P^3 + (ae+bf+d)P^2 + af \cdot P}{eP+f}$

Here: $A = c_0 c_3$, $B = c_0 + c_1 c_3$, $C = c_1 + c_2$, $D = c_3$, $E = 1$.

We need: $A/D = c_0$ (coefficient relationship), and we have 4 free constants ($c_0, c_1, c_2, c_3$) to match 4 GT parameters. This should work.

GT denominator: $7.531P + 1$, so $c_3 = 7.531$, $E = 1$ ✓.
GT numerator coefficient of $P^3$: $be = c_0 \cdot 7.531$
GT: $be = (-0.01095)(7.531) = -0.08243$ (approximately), so $c_0 = -0.08243/7.531 = -0.01095$.

Actually, let me just verify the structure matches. We have $\frac{AP^3+BP^2+CP}{DP+1}$ with free A, B, C, D. The GT is $\frac{\alpha P^3 + \beta P^2 + \gamma P}{\delta P + 1}$ (after normalizing). So yes, this matches.

**Candidate 27 verdict: [MATCH]**

### Candidate 50:
$$\frac{c_0 P^3 + (c_2+c_3)P^2 + c_4}{P+c_1} + c_5$$

$= \frac{c_0 P^3 + (c_2+c_3)P^2 + c_4 + c_5(P+c_1)}{P+c_1}$

$= \frac{c_0 P^3 + (c_2+c_3)P^2 + c_5 P + (c_4+c_5 c_1)}{P+c_1}$

For f(0)=0: $(c_4+c_5 c_1)/c_1 = 0$, so $c_4 = -c_5 c_1$.

Then: $\frac{c_0 P^3 + (c_2+c_3)P^2 + c_5 P}{P+c_1}$

This has 4 free parameters ($c_0, c_2+c_3, c_5, c_1$). Matches the GT structure.

**Candidate 50 verdict: [MATCH]**
